de la char sor le neis
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 No matter how many different types of hard growths appear, some resembling spider legs at various points; and if there are such or have flesh hues with furious colors, and soft flesh tones.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 For those cases of such growths that are soft and not inflamed, have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; clean their nostrils, squeeze out the lymph from these tissues, and rub furrows; cover it with a cloth stretched on a slender bone-like structure until you know that this growth is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be removed, work on all subtle veins lightly until nothing is left; and if the patient becomes swolculed or an abscess appears, treat them accordingly; and if it's malignant, haste to cauterize until they are completely excised and turned into bones, then pour oil or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If it does not work and moisture reaches the palate, understand that it is healed; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is decay in the bone above, which prevents pulling: then you must gently insert a linen thread slightly thickened by hand, leaving space between each knot; place the patient's head under the thread with some strength, and pull gently until it comes out through the mouth; this method has been used for children in schools many times, and is an easy task for those who perform it; then hold one cheek which emerges from beneath by one hand, and the other cheek which protrudes from the mouth with the other hand, while carefully observing each one as we do with our own thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do as much as you know that the worms have infected that vein, then draw out the blood, squeeze out the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian salve, and place it back in its nose as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointments corrode all that is attached to the vein; and then put a bandage on the nose for many days until healed, and if there's need of dry medicines, use them; and this is the tool used to purge the head, through which one distills oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or glass, resembling an open lamp similar to a flame, and you guide them the same way; and if you see one needs it, make it closed with no protrusions for purging the head; and have one hand holding the head when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease arises in the head of the neck called "telul", which grows and becomes large until it is visible to the eye; therefore, one must cut it at the beginning, and the bone entirely, then apply the cautery or burning medicine on it; if not done quickly before it becomes too large, be vigilant that it may be hard, of a strange color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as it is an incurable boil, for whenever one cuts it even once, the patient suffers greatly; and if the boil is from a tender spot, not of a strange color, then you see that you can completely cauterize it, so relieve the patient and do not fear, and treat drying things and tightening.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck is cut and sutured.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when there is a continuation of discharge from one of these sinew-covered wounds, it brings little benefit and may occur in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Thus when this occurs in anyone, first check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring together both edges into a seam, and treat until it heals; and if the edges are torn apart on either side, ensure you scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then join both edges into a seam, bind, and powder with dragon's blood powder, and burn incense; and place over the powders a piece of aloeswood from a strong or other type, leave it to work through itself, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you gather the solutions: by needles, as we have said in the abdominal suturing; or by thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	For abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the lips have an abscess that is hard like grains of barley and are small to larger in size; then you must turn the lip apart, split them at each spot, grasp with forceps on each side, place the leeches therein for each part; after the incision with vitriol pus flows out until it is cleaned away; then apply a soothing ointment and treat the lips until they are dry.
de la char des gencives	From the edge of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often it arises under the gums from being pushed backward, which the ancients called "albulus"; if necessary, support it with forceps, and cut to its root, allowing blood or pus to flow; then apply vitriol salt on the wound or other drying powders; and if that edge returns after cutting, and often this happens, second time cauterizing: it does not return after cautery; these are forms of abscesses to treat.
des sordens	Of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	in ousle chiktustsd
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating the tooth of its pain, take time to extract it as much as you can, for one must not leave any part behind; for it is a matter so high that there is no excuse for leaving any remnants.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient's mouth is strained by chewing, make sure to check for any broken teeth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the pain troubled the patient, and he thought it was an abscess or a toothache, and drew out the bad tooth; however, the pain did not leave due to this, until the evil thing is pulled, for we have seen this with such cases before; and when you are certain about the aching tooth, one must scrape around the tooth as much as possible, strongly warding off the gum from all sides; then move it back and forth a little bit at first and second using delicate tweezebits until it is well aligned, then firmly secure with the tweezers; and let the head of the shoulder be in your hands between thine joints, so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth directly with a break, if it does not fall out, take any of these tinctures and put them inside each part lightly, and move it as you did first.

And if the tooth is pierced and infected, it must be filled with bandages where the holes are; and gently strain it using pliers so that it does not break when extracted; one must carefully work around the gums to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And make sure that you do not break it and leave a piece behind, as this may cause the patient greater pain from the root's wickedness.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And be aware not to do as ignorant surgeons do, who through their haste and boldness often break the jaw without inserting anything we have mentioned; they bring great maladamia from the abscesses that remain in the roots or from the jaws they break, as we have often seen; and when extracting a tooth, wash the area with wine or oil and honey paste; if bleeding occurs there (which often happens), apply a broth of white lead; and if this does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the molars where teeth first move should have sharp points and large cheeks so that they do not double when you pull out a tooth. Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	They should have large bodies such that they do not bend when extracted, and be well-made of iron, with teeth to grip it firmly.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root stays on the path, it is necessary to place a piece of cotton soaked in butter there for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 As long as the tooth is smoothed, put in pincers called 'allefre', which make the head appear like a surgeon's spoon; and they are made inside just like a file.

Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	is they s.

et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments used before on teeth and of this instrument which appears to be large pliers, its form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and so f.

Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the natural course of the body, and its shape is unsightly, especially in young women, it must be determined whether there are nerves behind the tooth and if they are not on the right side, and cannot be felt or filed down: then scrape; and if there is a root with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is shown here, resembling .i. small beak, made of iron that has been sharpened at both ends.

et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole. quant li dent lochent	When the teeth become loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the tooth is loose due to knocking or falling out, and the patient cannot press on what they chew without it causing pain, you have treated them with medicines that restrict movement, but this does not help; if necessary, restrain with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and corrodes, but gold never changes. The wire should be of medium thickness according to the space between the teeth; and when aligning the teeth, take the thread and place it double between the two healthy teeth first, then insert the heads of the pincers between the teeth if there are one or more, until you securely reach the other health caregiver's side. Then continue covering up to where you started, and gently pull with your hand until they do not move; ensure a firm grip at the root of the loose tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then grasp the head of the thread with pliers, and join them together, positioning between a healthy tooth, ensuring it does not touch the tongue; then leave it so tight as long as it can stay, if it dislocates or moves, straighten with another thread. If it remained in place, it will serve throughout its life, forming the shape of two teeth and figures resembling two healthy molars:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is set loose, it is put back in its place repeatedly as we have said; only those who are wise and patient should be involved, never attempting the shape of a wolf's bone, placing it where it lacks, tightening it just as we have said, remaining long in this manner.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	And cut off the cord of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 At no time is this jawbone that comes from nature or wounds placed so; it may be created due to accidental injuries and the procedures are as follows: work on the mouth of the patient, ensuring its head remains intact and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve tie wide until the tongue is dislocated from its place, if there is swelling or hardness, treat promptly for wounds with a forceps and cut the wider ties; ensure that the fracture is not too open near the artery below it. After you have done this, lift up water-soluble material and soak it in cold or lukewarm water, then place a linen tent under the tongue of the patient; each night treat them with herbs such that sleep may be had.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 If bleeding continues, apply saltpeter to the wound; and if there is no healing, use the long caustic for treatment, which is good for this; then treat with another remedy until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez. des apostemes de la gorge	For boils in the throat

li chapistres des apostemes	The surgeons of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many kinds of abscesses, as recalled in this book from one to another, and they differ between perforation and cutting; and there are two ways, one being the same kind but due to moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for boils that occur within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 Because abscesses in the head are different from those at the base, and abscesses within muscles differ from those that occur in joints, each has its own judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if to an abscess one should not pierce until it is fully matured according to its development; and for those that require piercing when they are ripe, and do not mature as usual, like abscesses close to joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When abscesses appear near joints, and they are left to rot there, sometimes the ligament and nerve of the joint become corrupted, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 When an abscess is near the main body part, and if you delay its perforation until it dies out, it will harm the main body part; or if it's near the base, pierce there as soon as possible before it dies; however, do not pierce an abscess that has not completed digestion yet, except for those near the base, ensuring they do not perish in vain and become extended inside, leading to a fistula; and cannot be healed quickly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be known the time of abscess perforation when healing is complete, and this is when pain is alleviated, fever subsides, and reduction in pain and redness occurs, along with debilitation and sharpening of the headache from the abscess, and other signs; and it must be that you place the abscess perforation to depend on its location relative to the abscess, and where movement is possible. The perforation should be long in the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, joints, nerves, arteries, in all similar cases without swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those cases where they are dislocated, with the concerned limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in its chronic stage, it should be allowed to drain until complete digestion has occurred, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you puncture it in front of this, the toxin from within may spread through his body and he becomes filled with much filth; and sometimes the lips harden and the deepest parts.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there are abscesses that can be felt over a wide part of his body, according to what the limbs require.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure. And for those that have been split into three angles or punctured like a reed's sheath, and others that are shaped like other types of fistulas; and if there is round cutting, other cuts, and similar forms.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no head, as if an abscess appears superficially, it should be pierced easily; and when the abscess is large, and has a great swelling, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus at once, but drain part of it; then cauterize the abscess until the next day, then cease draining anything further; do this increasingly more each time until the swelling is completely reduced; especially if the patient is weak in virtue, or women bearing children, or small children, or elderly men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the arrows sometimes leap at the time of pus release; it may happen that it kills the patient, and do not be dismayed by this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 First of all handle this treatise with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, open the wound, and check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a neat size, prepare some tents made of linen or old cotton; and if it's large abscesses, with many pores, then in each one put a tent so they press against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess an area around the skin, fill it with old cotton or wool from linen cloth without moisture, and tie until the third day; then see the doctor, and treat with ointment until healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 When bleeding occurs at your wound site, treat with cold and soothing water, and apply a damp cloth, placing it over the area multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the bleeding persists, treat it properly and with care, using the powders mentioned in this book, especially if it is winter or the affected area or abscesses are very sensitive; then you should apply damp tents and cloths soaked in wine and warm oil; if it's summer, and the swoln areas are fleshy, you should use moistened clothes with cold water and oil, or wine and cooling oil until the third day, as we have said; then release the abscesses, drain them, and treat them accordingly until they heal.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And you must know this universally for treating abscesses: here is what I have told you about how to proceed with the treatment of abscesse, and now comes the chapter.
des soros	About pus. (The word "des" in Old French can mean both "of" or "from", so it's often a matter of context)
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 When small abscesses come to the head and are handled like linen threadworms, just as shears on a young sheep, there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that have fat and substances with moisture like hairs; and there are others that are hard and painful to cut, without any doubt if the arrow does not go against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is such that you try with every instrument called 'intrusive', from which the form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Because if it contains moisture, they go up along the long. (Note: The translation is not entirely clear due to missing context or possible errors in the original text.)
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And the cut above a bloody abscess and wet area is more lightweight, for there is little blood involved.

And if of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and of such abscesses that I capped from the head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and pus-filled, and could not break it; and had one struck it, they would have made just as well a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or heads that come from the head of children and at the roots of ears, the opening should be as wide as possible on the day it is opened so they can release pus; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	the f h. Manze de lapeccest c's.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the shoulders, and in the armpits, never appearing elsewhere or on limbs, and they are very large, and closely related to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula properly comes from a dense spot on the body, just as lumps and abscesses in the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and others which are of an evil nature and do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In those cases then where you see good disposition at the touch and is similar to the body's color, and it moves freely on all sides without being near the nerves in the neck or arteries or ducts, and not deep; one must cope with it from above, peel off each part, and extend the two lips of the skin like incised wounds if necessary as we have said in head abscesses; and tear out little by little, being sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, nor be there any spatula or scalpel so that the hand slips away.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 If you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, then apply vitriol paste on the wound or powders that remain blood, hold the wound; let it rest until the abscess is soothed, softened, and begin to decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the blood has ceased flowing, return to your work until you complete it; then follow with your usual method if there are no small tumors remaining, remove and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein in the root of the tumor, you should not cut that tumor at its base but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang without harm; then treat the wound with cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then dress it.

And if you remove the entire scrofula, it is necessary to join the two edges of the wound and sew them up without leaving excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 If necessary, you must expose and remove the root (of the disease), pull out any pus-filled abscesses, and close up as we have previously described.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Scrofulas that retain excess fluid should be pierced where it is most swollen; and treated similarly to those previously mentioned, with applications of ointment and similar substances if there is a risk of decay within the retained matter; and once the wound is thoroughly cleansed, apply healing salve oil until completely cured.
de squinance	Of quinsance
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the throat incision; but I never saw it done in our land, and it is through their writings that we know of this.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with quinsy, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat called "epiglottis" be cleared; and you cannot aid by this method because all the veins and the main part of the malaise are at a boil in cases of abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the main part, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 It is necessary, when we wish to split the epiglottis, that we fracture it from above three circles or four along with a small slit across, between two circles or by the quantity of the slit on the side; and those lice are agreeable to the section of the epanglote so there is no choking, and the veins remain long in place.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is fearful, it must be extended with the leather of the throat to its full length, then cut through until reaching the joint; and drain the veins, if you see anything, and then cover the wound as we have said; and proven by the bleeding from the fistula that bursts out through the gap which is broken, and due to the loss of voice; and leave the open wound exposed.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the time has passed for doubting a strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound so that they are joined; then apply remedies which promote healing and make it whole until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Not until the throat is completely blocked will you do this; and if the patient appears to be dying, and lacks breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then take the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe out, and he breathes through the wound, thus preventing death; and they command the physician to leave the open wound until the illness has passed, which is in 3 or 4 days, then they instruct to sew up the wound and clean it, until it is cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a maiden took a knife and stabbed it into her throat, cutting parts of the windpipe under the jaw; and I went to be called to cure her, but found her just as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found blood issuing from it, but was well that it had not caused swelling or a tight band to choke the throat; however, there was severe bleeding through the injury.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried, sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and within the maiden there came no change in her voice, and she returned to normal afterwards; therefore I say that in treating the epiglottis one should have no fear.
de la grosse gorge	From a swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "throat hernias," and they are large abscesses in the color of jet, and occur mostly in women; and there are two ways: natural and accidental; where nature has no influence.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 The accidental type is of two kinds: one resembling fatness in us, and the other kind resembles an abscess that comes from us through arteries; there is fear, and it should not be operated on with force unless it is small, and you test and search for all involvement: if you find it similar to our fatness, and not extending to any vein, then bandage as you would a wound, and treat throughout its entirety, if necessary; and examine thoroughly, and heal as required until perfectly healthy.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 There are many ways we do things, of which I will tell all the resemblances; and now it must be said what the differences are between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is heat and fever-bearing, as long as the boiling persists, and decay is complete; then rests the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With us there is no fever or pain, and we contain pus, which is our own sacer and follows the body's natural color; it begins like a drop of wax and grows; and they resemble two things, either grains or moisture, and many colors as I have said in my division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When attending to this matter, first examine and inquire about the entire instrument called "entromissor," according to its form or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of inquiring about abscesses in us is to grasp or make them more moist where you find the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little until you know that the swelling has been felt underneath, then extract the interposing matter; be cautious so it does not burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs through the vein and it has a color as I have mentioned with other boils; and if after inserting the entromission there is no moisture, assume that it is greasy, then pierce accordingly in a cross pattern and take it with forceps, gently scraping from all sides while keeping the coat intact where it lies, treating it cleanly with the needle; and if you cannot treat it cleanly, cut it into pieces so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If nothing remains after it has been removed many times and if a small amount remains and the sinus is not painful, apply to the wound with corrosive powders such as acid sponges, compress the wound, and apply soothing ointments for other treatments until it heals; and if they are large, cut around the edges of the wound, and treat what causes infection.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	If it is contrary or another urgency occurs and you hastily apply the lead of vitriol paste, leave it for two days or three, until the wound heals, then allow the bleeding to subside; afterwards return to its original state as was delayed before.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See here the forms of inserted intestines, and they are in three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are also in three ways: large, medium, and small, to explore boils of fistulas; and they are like the needles with which one treats witches, and they come in citrin silver or iron, or gold, and those moved by water value as those that are yellow, and more tested for black pus exploring abscesses of fastoids; and there are also in three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the pores.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of cancer are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and those with ulcers in three ways alike; and those with ulcers in three ways and they too come in three manners; and those with two ulcers, and cancers with a single ulcer only, and they too appear in three forms; all these are necessary in their own place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these tools that are cutting come sharp and some which do not cut but one part, from which the skin is scraped so that neither veins nor nerves are severed; and the intermediaries with loops reset in fists, such that the patient does not become visible at the onset of abscesses. There are three manners: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are never used except in joints like legs, arms, nipples, elburtons, and others, and sometimes a small instrument similar to fistula scrapings is made according to this form, by which blood is stopped.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And you put it back into place at times with blood flow from veins, and arteries, and sometimes they return according to this major form:

dou chancre	Of a canker

de l’estopement de la verge	For the stopping of the vein
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 There is never a child born without testicles, or if the testicles are small, they may not be in their proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it is necessary soon that he cannot pierce all parts of the scrotum very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.
