And the manner of its use is that the patient lies supine with their head elevated and the penis lengthened like a feather's stem; and be careful to prevent excessive blood loss which often occurs, and if it does happen, apply the tourniquet for controlling bleeding, and treat the wound until healed.
des pustules de la verge	From boils of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these swellings in the penis, and it appears as an ugly growth; there are malignant and benign ones; thus you must pluck them with a fine needle, then cleanse and wash all thoroughly, then apply cotton soaked in refined Egyptian ointment, curing with this ointment until they heal.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the boil is malignant, of foul color and draining pus, one must apply a fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 Once you have approached it, and if the boil is on the shaft of the penis, having part inside the hair and part further down, one must remove the boil that is within first; and once it is split open, cleanse the lower part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you treat it together, make sure the head of the penis is not perforated, and darkness and decay come to its channel or base; then address all that is blackened and corrupted, followed by applying a poultice on the navel made from the bark of red apples and dates, then continue with other treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, prepare a lunar cautery according to this method:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery serves two purposes together: namely, to stop bleeding and to address corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must insert or guide a tube into the penis and urinate within it for the patient; and if hairs are present on the top of the penis which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, whether due to injury or an abscess, then indeed you should scrape it with a sharp instrument until all fibrous tissue is removed, freeing the head of the penis from all sides; and if this is a serious matter, then you should gently scrape near the top of the penis and hairs with a spatula for some time; then carefully separate them both, and place a delicate linen cloth soaked in cold water between them without fully detaching.
de la circoncision	Regarding circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the dislocation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our will and properly for children, it is necessary that we make the best and easiest work for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say the ancients did not mention child circumcision, as they do not practice it in their laws, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greater part of masters and authorities who performed circumcision within one day, and at all times, and in every manner; there were keys because there are two locks, and by chance a cap was placed above and below those locks.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Then it is regained by pressure, and the pain doubles, and with the redness which is half due to cold, the tip of the limb is not fully secure; and sometimes during the trimming of the nail, the steel escapes from them, causing wounds, and many times they come about without needing further treatment.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the mundification performed using force throughout the entire line of thread, I have found the benefit of experimentation, as the forces cut exactly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you press your hand, make it equal in strength throughout; but the child must be well restrained inside the leather; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if they understand, that you are only tying a thread around the penis for some time, then allow them to breathe in all manners possible; then keep it straight between your hands, and bring back the forces between your hands or below your feet so the child does not see any of it, nor any movements; then place your hand on the rod and blow or snuff, and draw it up until the head of the rod is out; then cleanse well from any filth that has gathered there, then tie a double thread at the knot, then tie below one stitch to another loop; and hold them together with two loops by the pouchet and index finger, keeping between the two loops, then quickly remove the snuff and lift the head of the rod; then let blood drip slowly because it is freshly made; and put powder on and over it, glued with a small half egg yolk cooked without leavening mixed with rose water, blended with good and fresh oil, and leave it until the next day, and cure further until it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the chisels for this procedure is as follows: the two heads should be held and sharp, and each head should be as large as a hand evenly.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the procedure is when the core escapes during the incision; therefore, you must extend it with your fingernail so that the edges make an opening, and then cut evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, use pincers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it passes three days and what is beneath the rod is swollen, leave it until the incisions have healed, and gently scrape away; cut as you can move, but protect the part of the penis, for this will not cause any harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat then the sudden pain of powder wounds that we have discussed in our treatment of powders, and if one copes with it excessively causing it to go too high, do not harm; treat as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Regarding urinary retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to a blockage of stones, frozen blood or thorns, or other similar things that we have discussed in the division; and if the urine is not retained, and you see the obstruction caused by a stone located either near or at the neck of the bladwook, it should be made for the patient to lie on his elbows with feet placed on his back, and extend his abdomen upwards towards the upper back; and then he must press against the chest as much as possible. And afterwards, you constrain the bladder neck to expel the stone through urine from above, causing the urine to flow freely out; and if it does not come out, where we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it should be managed with extraction using a device called "catheter", of which here is the form: made of finely worked silver wire as light as a bird's feather; and let its length be about half a palm.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 The method of draining the urine is such that you take a double thread and tie it to a small piece of wool or cotton at one end, then place the head through the hollow of the syringe; trim any excess wool/cotton and insert until just below the tip of the saturator, then grease the saturator with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a stool, while you apply oil-moistened olive oil and water to the bladder and penis, then gently insert the saturator into the penis until it reaches near the root of the penis, then pull the foreskin towards the scrotum; then fill the saturator up to the bladwoid with urine, which you will sense as the patient feels relief and empties themselves, provided that the device is not twisted in its movement; then extract the thread until all wool/cotton remains, after which urine follows along the string; finally remove the saturator and drain the urine. Repeat this process with the saturator as long as the bladder needs to be emptied and comfort is restored to the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Concerning diseases of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When stitches or blood reaches the bladder, where swelling has accumulated, and you see it to be drained with waters and medicines, do so using all the instrument called "clamps", which is its form.
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and if it has three openings: two from one side, and one from the other, as you see; and the vessel above which the medicine poultice is placed so that it well covers the penis without additional substance, if moisture can be expressed, and inserted where necessary; and when you see your medicines in the bladder, place the knife of a barber on the moisture, and express at the tube which is there; through this method, moisture will be extracted using the funnel, then firmly reinsert the tube; moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the subtle form of the enema for cleansing the bladder: as follows.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 Silver or lead is used, and the head is higher; from behind at the neck do the ligaments detach; then take an ox bladder and place it in water to be used for enema administration through the bladroids, then tie them together with a good double thread, heat that moisture over fire; then pour the head into the enema tube, then tighten your hand around the bladder allowing all the moisture to enter quickly until the patient feels the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make one circle, and pierce it roundly through; then thread a strong filament into these holes, then assemble the circle as one would assemble flax, and put within what you wish with oil and moisture and water, and tie in the instrument; and do so as if done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division of stone removal methods and extraction with medicines; we have described the difference between stones caused by rain, and all signs, and which type of stone requires cutting; and for bladder stones, and for penile stones; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stones which are caused by the bladabladder often occur in children and it is a sign that the water of the bladder seems to flow as clear water; and there's an earthy smell, and the male suffers great pain in his penis, and he urinates many times before becoming enlarged; and with such stones, the foundations are greatly affected. It is much easier for children up until they have 4 years old to be cured, it is most severe in older men, and moderate between youths and elderly; and the treatment of those who have large stones is easier than that of those who have small stones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 When we come to treat them, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the feces from within the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 Because it always hinders one's ability to urinate.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and stand them upright so that the stone descends to the opening of the bladder and emerges without difficulty from below; then make the patient sit between your hands properly, with their hands behind their thighs so that the bladder is fully inclined downward; then aim and touch inside; if you feel the stone in place, proceed immediately with dilating it.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not pass through touching at all, grease your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child or has a median fissure; and push in its base, aim for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, press toward the neck of the bladaderetainer. Then release pressure on your finger, and let it fall out where you saw fit to dilate it.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	The patient instructs the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands that he extend upwards with his right hand the joints, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the joints in the area where circumcision is made; then he applies the spatula copingly, which forms:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And it forms between the one who is between the joints and the foundation, neither too far nor to the left of the nape, but right above the stone; and it should be level with the waist or base, and level from side to side, and let the width be wide in front for convenience, and narrow inside according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps apply pressure so that the sides are without effort; and know that there may be a piece of stone or corners and edges: these need to be removed; and if it is at eye level, similar to glass, and round, from which removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Where there are angles and edges, make the opening larger; and if it cannot be separated, then you must use forceps like they would with a lime at the tip to remove the stone so that it does not escape outwards; or strike from below using a delicate instrument curved at the top; and if you cannot manage this way, widen the opening slightly, and if it's narrowed by scarring, apply vinegar for straining; and if there are more than one stone, first remove the largest at the bladder neck, then upwards, then straight forward, and any smaller ones afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 If it is very large, one must sew it up, causing a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For there are two things that happen to the patient: they die or urine flows in due to the eyes being unable to heal properly; nonetheless, strive with the drainage and cauterization using tongs until you have drained by pieces; when you have completed your work, treat the wound with incense, aloe, dragon's blood, and bandages, and oil a cloth in oil or wine, or rosewater and cold water to cool the ulceration; then return the patient to his bed, without removing the bandage until after three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, the place is greatly filled with oil and water, then treat with diaphoretic ointment and basil ointment until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if an abscess comes in the wound and erosions, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and it is retained due to this, preventing urine flow, which is known by its incomplete passage with urine: then place your finger in the wound, extract that blood, for if it remains, the bladder will be affected, and weakened; then cleanse the wound of water and debris and hairs, and assist it in all ways you can, until it is healthy again; and it is necessary to tie both thighs when treating this, and apply medicines at its location.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small and located in the urethra, protruding outwards, preventing urine from passing; treat it as I have described before, by dilating many times with a tool designed for this purpose.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already found such a thing to be this way.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron rod according to this shape and be at three pointed ends sharpened into one tip.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take the wire and loop it around the shaft below the stone, ensuring that it cannot come back into the bladder; then insert the needle lightly into the shaft until reaching the stone; and rotate the needle slowly to your hand on the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce through the other side of the stone; urine will come out shortly thereafter, then press with your hand where it remains inside the stone within the sheath.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken so quickly and escapes with the urine, leaving the patient relieved; and if you cannot do this due to any obstacle, then take a wire below the stone and another above, then make the sheath at the place between the two wires where the stone is, then extract the stone forcefully, remove the ligatures, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; treat it until it is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	Of women's pierced areas.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Often, piercing occurs in women's bodies, and if it does so infrequently, then the treatment is difficult for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman may be a virgin; and secondly, there may not be found a well-informed woman who will expose herself at the bathhouse, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third way is that sometimes one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that if the stone from the woman is more embedded than the man's, it requires making a deeper incision with great fear involved. And if necessary to remove it by such means, then you must call upon a skilled midwife without delay, and if you cannot find one, seek out a very subtle female healer; present a well-informed woman who knows part of the craft or a woman knowledgeable in some aspect of it, commanding her to perform the stone examination as instructed. Then ensure that the woman is a virgin: then she must position herself properly and locate the stone; if found, she must be restrained away from her lower parts, advising her to place her hand or knee firmly against the bladder with urging and pressure using her left hand.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is dislocated, gradually move it from near the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then press on the stone at the thigh's root towards the middle of the leg where it becomes misaligned, and feels the stone in that area; do not move its joint above or below the stone, and apply a small force initially. Then place your weight onto the buttocks if you feel the stone so that the wound can heal as much as possible until the stone may come out, and know there are many types of stones: they are small and large and sharp and smooth, long and round, with veins.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you recognize them to understand their nature.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 If the stone is not won, then put boiled alum at its place, and hold it for an hour until it becomes firm; then return to your work as long as the stone remains strong, and apply linen bandages as I have told you in the removal of stones from horses to aid you in your task; if the stone is not won and it's a vein that has burst, put powder at its place and bind with tents and bandages, do not attempt again without risking death, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the joint rests, return to your work as long as the wound is strong.
de hernie carnouse	line:
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Immediately after washing, it is nothing but a gathering of moisture or pus beneath the skin near the joints, which is contained within the vein; and it is called "pus," and never properly in the tissue of the vein, as one might think it to be another vein; and it is the leather-like substance between the white pus that we have mentioned earlier; and this does not happen at all.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the production of this gathering is due to weakness in the joints, and that material is spread there.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 Never from percussion on the joints comes this moisture: its color declines to jaundice, or without redness, blackness, or very white, and it occurs more frequently; these are signs of knowing what congregation has come, for if it is as we have said, whitish facies, then the abscesses are reasonable, not long like an egg's shape, and do not open the joints, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 If there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the boil seems connected with part of the fat, and for this reason it is thought to be another organ; and if the moisture is between the skin and subcutaneous tissue, then it feels very well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine thoroughly in all directions as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intervention, judge according to what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we treat it with iron, one must ensure the patient is healthy and well-nourished as much as possible; then place them on their back over something slightly elevated, and cover them abundantly with cloths; then move to their left side, and command the attendant that they sit to the right, and extend a rod to one of the two lower ribcage bones; then take the spatula blade, and separate the skin between it along its length up to near the wrist joint, and make your incision straight as you navigate through the skin until reaching white fatty tissue, and carefully scrape off the superficial layer; then pierce the fat cleanly with a wide bore, and extract all the fluid, then apply bandages, and elevate the fat; but do not touch the bones of the ribcuge, only the fat. Carefully or in pieces as needed remove the fibrous tissue from around them so that if you don't cut cleanly, the fluid will return; and if the abscess bursts at your handiwork, then stitch up both sides of the bone overlying it when you have completed the procedure on the fat. Then treat as other wounds until they are healthy again.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the sac affected by another illness, it is necessary to tie up the veins that are hanging loosely, suspecting blood leakage; then cut through the ribcage completely and remove the sac, and treat it as we have described.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if the fracture is joined in two parts together, you know they are branches; so join the other part as you did with the first equally, then drain the blood, and apply greasy linen to the wound; and provide another layer of moistened linen soaked in wine and oil, and place on both ends, and cover with doubled cloths, securing it above all connected tissue according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths and place scraps of cotton according to this pattern and sew them together over the waistline of the trousers; one head reaches from the foundation up to the back, and the other goes towards the part where the fingers are located. The other pair covers both elbows, and all is securely fastened in a loop with the pants. And on no occasion should this treatment with fire be used as an alternative for iron cutting; instead, you use the finer cautery instrument. Remove the leather from the joints, and let them scald as we have said, so that the white fascia containing the blood is exposed. Then take the cautery in accordance with this pattern, puncture at the nodes, and scrape it off using this fine hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 In all ways you can hold the cup so that you touch everything; and ensure the fire does not touch the skin; and know this work is more healing; and with careful attention to blood flow, and movements of cutting; and if anything contrary happens such as abscesses or bleeding abnormalities or other things, treat what goes against it, according to what has been previously said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this treatment due to its severity, then proceed with perforation as I instruct; provided that you are well convinced by the meanings we have said about draining being necessary, make the patient sit on a chair lifted up; then pierce the abscess in the part opposite of all surrounding fat, and place the puncture deep into the body; ensure the openings are wide so that water flows freely. Then put cotton over it, secure with bandage, allowing for the rest of the liquid to drain out; then treat until the wound is healed; if a cloth does not allow fluid to escape through the wound's mouth, you must insert a cannula or the instrument used for treating dropsy as previously described; enlarge the wound and know that the liquid returns, reassembling after six months or sooner. When it has reformed as before, this way the patient will recover their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of boils
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 In this part of the treatise on wounds are various complications that cause fear in many, which is why I believe it should be left alone; and I will tell you about the procedure and the appearance of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Thus, I say that many abscesses come from the body, especially in the thighs; and this happens quite often.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It is known that by excessive bitterness and chillness, which spreads to the joints or from percussion; and the color of an abscess depends on the person's complexion; there is no pain, and it is a severe abscess; and sometimes it can be dangerous pus-filled and piercing abscesses with fluctuating colors, and never comes from our arteries or vein swelling.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is from our artery, you can recognize the nature of an abscess by how hot it feels when pressed with your hands; and it does not require that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 He who is inflamed with veins can be recognized by his tendency to pain upon touching the joints, and he may well make an incision on this swelling, and others; then clip off the head of the gland, then extend it upward, and treat the white fascia therein, releasing all parts of the gland.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the gland is already softened by these nodes, then you must incise and clip it; if there are adhesions in the fascia, or within the vessels, then you should release all that tissue entirely, rounding off the clipping.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the birthmark is behind or in place, it must be covered entirely and remove the wool as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	, and it the is rense avoir that you to cest l'orent li nt the tissage. de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of boils
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess swathed in a wrapping resembling a bud, with the softening of tissues, and it moves greatly when touched; the treatment for this disease is as perilous as that before, and we will tell you its workings according to what was done by the ancients.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 You must make the patient sit on the bed elevated, then wrap the suspensory cord around his knees, all the straps close to the waist, and tie them tightly; next, cut the sharp spatula wide at a place between the legs, until they are uncovered, then scrape each side as we have explained in the extraction of arteries found in temples; then insert a needle where it has double thread, and attach it to the first spot where the vein emerged, and tie it securely at the other end; next, cut the cord straight according to the length of the body, and drain any corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as with other bow injuries, ensuring no vessels are left unnourished from either leg; because by this means there is no harm, and wherever veins emerge in all limbs, it is necessary to drain them according to each one.
de la routure dou syfac	Of sore festering
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The developments of this branch are by section that comes from punching or swelling in the abdomen near the elbangs, causing intestines to be displaced; and this displacement is either from punching or extension, and these two methods come from various causes: punches, jumps, screams, lifting heavy weights, etc.; when it comes to extension due to swelling, the signs are that it happens gradually over a long time and does not occur suddenly; and abscesses form equally toward the front because the swelling accelerates the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	When it comes to the signs of gangrenous sack severance, as sudden pain occurs at its onset and various abscesses appear near the skin surface, due to intestinal issue and gangrene in the body.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And at no time do they pass with the intestines, and are retained inside, causing great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	In these cases of iron treatment by fear, it is necessary to remove them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 The way of the treatment is that you command the patient to inspect the intestines with his hand inside the wound if he can reenter it; then wrap the buttocks between your hands, and lift them; next extend the head towards above, and cover all the skin around the ears equally; then insert hooks into the waist according to how many you need to open the wound, choosing ones that allow the oesophagus to come out; then scrape off the whitish swelling underneath the ear's skin until the hard swelling is exposed from all sides; then put your index finger in between which covers the ear and the second swelling, separating what lies behind the first swelling and between the second one; next move both ears towards your right hand inside the head cavity, raise up the whitish portion with your left hand toward the waist; and command a helper to extend it upwards, pulling away from any attachments in its rear part. And try to catch any intestine or hard swelling using your fingers if you find anything like that, then place it into the abdomen below; then take a needle with I thick filament made of X threads and insert it at the back end of the swelling which lies past the ear'veins; after the waist, cut any visible strings appearing from these vessels as long as there are IIII of them; then tie them up one on top of another in a cross shape, securing the swelling lying below the ears with a strong knot made out of two ends. Then wrap the threads and secure them both-sidedly so that no blood vessel can penetrate it otherwise an abscess may occur there; then place the knot according to the previous long one on each hand, followed by another set following the curvature of the oesophagus in its entirety. Then cut again in the area below the ear's skin until you reach bare muscle and bone as we have mentioned before; finally, clean with soaked cloth in oil then put into wounds, and apply the knot which we previously mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is the facial swelling cauterized as we have mentioned, after incision, due to fear of blood flowing out.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 This often happens, leaving the ligament to shrink on its own; and if it takes too long, raise with warm water as we have said before until it shrinks; then treat the wound as usual until it is perfectly healed.

En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this treatment, I have never seen anyone who dared to undertake the remedy with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like a joint held together by ligaments, in such a way that you bind the vessels after cutting slightly above the base; then cover with honeycomb and treat the abscess of what works there until it shrinks; and treat it as we have described, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 It never comes to an obstruction within the groin, as we have described, and it does not protrude any of the intestines from the joints, and if they do protrude, it is minor and resolves quickly; however, if it persists too long in this point, there will be a tear or swelling of the intestine causing them to protrude again because it is extended within the groin as we have described, since it is stretched, then the skin becomes soft and inflamed at the opening and open; and you treat it with cautery as we have previously said: and in no case is it treated by iron in this manner: where the patient lies on his back between your hands, then cover the swoln area of the protrusion according to the quantity of three strings; then extract the hernia that lies underneath the skin covering, then take hold of the tail and place it over the open hernia; press at the center of the belly, then cut both visible parts of the hernia near its head with a razor, cutting one and the other; then you extract the head with the razor, but do not cover the swelling or extend anything else, as I have instructed in the treatment of intestinal groin joints; then treat it as usual for wound care.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you bind the wounds, if they are swollen and treat the injury, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The face is swollen, has no appearance in the normal position, and the cautery moves easily at this spot, closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	For softening of the thick skin of the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the joints is softened in certain individuals because their bursae are moisturized and appear transparent; when curing it, you must lay the patient on his back with the affected area exposed, and cut the overlying loose skin from its natural skin, then sew the two lips together along a single line or four lines firmly; between these stitches, treat as you would other wounds until they are healed, and extract any pus.
dou chastrement	By means of cauterization
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 This knowledge of shearing is removed from our law, and I would not like to discuss it in this book; however, it is necessary for two reasons: one is that the master responds with advice when asked about it, and its treatment; the other because we often need animal shearing (like goats, sheep, lambs, and other animals) to help us.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say therefore that shearing is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the method where we do shearing by attraction, make the animal sit in warm water until its wool is softened and pliant; then pluck with your hand, until it's replaced and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Regarding the tincturing by cutting: it is necessary to hold the animal, and press the hide of its joints in your left hand, then tie the suspensory muscle, and bind above each foot with a bandage after you have properly scorched them; and leave no part unbruised or any delicate sores on their limbs; this method of tincturing by cutting is more effective than that done by attraction, because in attraction the joints may remain undamaged causing the animal to desire copulation; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites: Those are individuals who possess both male and female sexual organs or characteristics, often seen as a medical anomaly in old texts. The translation should address this directly while maintaining sensitivity to modern understandings of gender diversity. Here is the line-by-line English translation for clarity:
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 A hermaphrodite is in two ways among the common folk: one where between its two testes it has an appearance like that of a woman's genitalia, or sometimes at times it urinates.

de la tentigene	Of tendentiousness
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Swelling is an adhesion in the natural part, too unsightly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its remedy.

de erratique	Of erraticness
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. de l’enfantement	When childbirth occurs: observe whether it is a normal delivery or difficult; provide comfort and assistance to the mother during labor; ensure cleanlinees tools and surroundings for safety of both mother and baby; assist with breathing techniques, position changes, and pain relief as needed. After birth, support the mother in bonding with her newborn, initiate breastfeeding if possible, and monitor their health closely.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Those who come otherwise do not come naturally.

The fire cautery brings together two things: that is, the burning of inflamed tissues and stopping blood loss, as well as drying moisture; then treating soiled bandages with butter or bread crumbs until they are completely burned away, and removing scabs on wounds caused by sudden oil spills in a hardened charred skin; then treating the ointment-induced blisters of a long-lasting sore.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When it is restored, it becomes healthy and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes near to the very foundation, and is distant from the body, you may touch your thumb or wrist, and examine it.

Allow waste matter to be expelled naturally at its own will; then heal it as we have instructed. Occasionally this may leave a clean wound, or remove any tissue near the base of the wound with a tool such as an incision knife or another device suited for it; next address the misplaced charred tissue in the wound to the best extent you can; then focus on restoring the wound and maintaining control over the fistula located beyond the foundation: this would be easier for the patient.

des emorroydes	To treat swollen glands, the following methods are used which we now explain to you; but do not forget what you heard before about various techniques of fire cautery.

dou fremit	And the trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A mole is a small fault near the body, and often hidden; never feels cold to touch, and seems dead with its trembling sensation, spreading throughout the entire body, especially in the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 The treatment is to take the shaft of an ostrich feather or a strong vulture quill and place it on the trembling area until the small circle becomes entirely numb; then turn your hand all around the shaft until you have thoroughly covered the entire trembling area, making sure it is exposed everywhere, and extract the root of the tremor.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see this tremor as a spider or iron of this form, and be subtle from below and crosswise above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not feel it, but keep hold of both [sides], and squeeze them; and if you see the tremor, then causticate it as before or with a fire cautery.

des plaies	Wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	As we have said in the section on wound care, now we will discuss treatments for hands and medicines according to their completion:
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and where they are located, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 Things by which wounds are made include piercing of stones, sharpening swords and knives or spears, lances, clubs, etc., or similar things; or they are done according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that bleeds from the neck, head, groin, abdomen, liver, and resembling limbs. And I will tell you the cure for each wound, beginning with simple head wounds, because memory comes back in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 When a simple wound or head injury occurs and the bone is not broken, be careful if it's from stone fall or similar causes, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound large, and you slightly suspect an abscess: immediately bandage the head area if there is blood from the wound, place the dressing opposite to the injured part; and prevent the patient from repletion of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy; it is that you place this powder which has been mixed with mercury (arsenic).
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 The manner of the powder is thus: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coal three parts, and grind finely, apply to the wound, firmly press so that it dries well and joins with all its blood; then bandage securely, and leave without unbandaging unless it swells.

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	t;t:s.

If it is a stab wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, then observe whether the patient exhibits signs of internal bleeding: understand that if the wound is mortal; but if it is not deep and is fresh throughout its blood supply, do not apply any powders in the first hour nor bind them to prevent the flow of blood into the body, lest it return to the heart and blind the patient; instead, apply an attractive ointment and bandage it twice a day; but if you have no ointment, place raw cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient sleep on their back over the wound for three days or more; this will prevent spasms or tremors of the body or abnormal retractions; and when you see favorable conditions, understand that the wound is healed.

Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.
