des voinnes dou cors communes	common body veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 Of veins that one can see are XXXI in total, of which the head is XVI, namely: two earrings located behind the ears called "herbeches"; and the two arteries visible on each temple; and the two veins found in the eyelids known as "aspires"; and the vein that runs across the forehead; and the vein at the nasal bridge; and the two tendrils located by the neck called "guindeges"; and the two veins found on each lip above the mouth, also referred to as "augeherichs"; and the two veins underneaturally, which is a part of the facial venous system.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly bled from each arm: one is cephalic, and located near the left side ribs, called by people "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast" and composed of cephalic and basilica, called by people "vein of the body"; the basilica is on the right side ribs, called by people "vein of the belly," and it's below the scapula, and that vein which is bled openly over the neck.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the salvator is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, with two branches; in the leg and at the ankle are three veins: one above the groove of the inner calf on the left side ribs, and the second femoral which is near the right ankle; and the vein called "saphena" that lies in the crease of the other ankle; and in the other leg there are three veins above those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The sickness of veins that are located behind the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and migraines; the quality of the treatment, as I've told you, is to raise the patient's head, and rub the area where the veins are with a coarse cloth; then tighten the neck with a twist until the two veins appear behind the ears in double layers: tie them at your index finger, and wherever you feel hair above your thumb, mark it; then take the lancet, cut to the bone below the vein, lift your hand all around the vein upwards, peel and clean both sides of the incision completely, and let blood flow until clear; then compress and tie until healed; as I've mentioned before, there is also an incision and cauterization from the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The source of the two arteries located in the temples, should be bruised to stop bleeding, gently but firmly and traditionally used for making tears at the eyes; and the quality of the tourniquet is as I say: it allows the patient to turn his neck until both veins appear openly; he feels pain on top of his ears, then dizziness follows; next place your thumb over the vein up by your index finger, and insert the lancet below, lift the vein up, and collect the blood as you have done with other veins, and let the blood flow according to necessity; afterwards release the patient, and put your elbow under the vein for an hour, then cover it with cotton; and compress firmly, leaving until healed. And we have spoken about their bandaging and extraction, beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The drainage of the vein at the front is as necessary as for the cephalic in old facial diseases, and migraines, and redness; and its quality is such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "sophoor," which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the tip over the vein, and hold it steady with your hand or another object, allowing blood to flow out in quantity that you see; then straighten the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is completely sealed and no bleeding occurs from a wide wound.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it should not be too tightly bound; and the sinew perpendicular to the bone, because the bone is near, and sometimes it breaks the sinew when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Draining of the two veins located in the temples helps with eyes, tinnitamoius, redness, vertigo, and facial diseases; its quality is such that the patient twists his neck without any ligature as before; then perform the drainage across the bridge, a bit long, slightly wide, because there is no pain.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And be the blood is well executed by skill and so does not die if you are skilled then done. Then it shall know wherefore, and do; Et en la morts; and so the art doute, car of as our lord, est de f in this place et flaime tant de tuit par le be a lieu, or l’artie, que li art du fait is sient les mallardien on.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The lining of the vein from the nose is good for gagging and suffocation, and facial illnesses such as migraines and redness that come on in the face, especially when they are old; and the quality of the vein lining is that it causes patients to tighten their neck, then strains the nose towards your left hand, and takes a long subtle breath, and inserts it halfway into the lip between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open fully, and blood will begin to flow now; do not insert too deeply, and let the blood flow according to necessity, then tie it off for one night, as it is quickly restored; this is the form of the breath.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The tension of the two muscles aids in stretching the artery, and at the beginning of surgery, and for many diseases, and scabs, and corrosion, and herpes, and itching; and the quality of the tension is such that the patient separates his neck from either side as we have said; and be seated over him with their head upwards, then cut a vein slightly wide for a while, then bleed the blood quickly, or as much as necessary; then again in another vein, then loosen the ligaments, and grip both veins moderately, so that the patient does not strain; and leave until morning when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the liver ailment called jaundice
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleaning of lice from the lips helps to clear infection in the mouth, and gum disease, and cracks on the lips, and bad breath and itching.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of jaundice are to have the patient sit before you and hold their neck as I have described; then turn the lip, and look into the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, recognizing them by being black and having small dark spots within: thus cut both, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the larger ones from each side, and likewise with those above and below, for they are of the same kind.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the jaundice underneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The jaundice of the veins underneath the tongue follows that of the headache, and it is in the widening of the throat, and eye diseases, and mouth diseases; and the qualities for treating this are having the patient cut between your hands in the sunlight and lifting the tongue, then looking down each side to see a black vein: thus cut both, but not too deeply, as underneath are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins of the arm that are commonly opened in practice are treated according to two methods: either by puncturing at any wide part, or with a slender and sharp tool like trepan, which is called "anesil"; and they are both wide and narrow depending on the width and extension of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of this mistletoe plant is much renowned and very broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary to open plain-skinned veins containing obvious and turbid blood, which are the form of the slender frame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is finer pointed, and meant for collecting subtle veins, where there is a subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The vein of the jugular, which is one such vein, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and where the collarbone, neck, and abdomen are; and it is appropriate for the cauterizer to treat vigorously and cleanse themselves of the artery located below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if you cut the artery, and bleeding begins, then it must be sealed as I have said; and it should not be bound too tightly by the bandage, but rather trimmed as one would pare a nail.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basin does not open clearly, then it must be extracted and another used; or you desire its rim without any flaw, or cleanse in place of it the vein within the arm: it opens clearly; and cut the bandage neatly as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you know the location of the lesion, then proceed to extract the arm, touching the area until you feel the hair; sign it with a bandage, and then lie down the arm, cut the vein neatly as before; be careful not to harm the artery when you see the area swelling, for it is an artery: thus escape.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If you see it bulging upward like a child's urine, and the vein is red and fine, know that it is from an artery: then quickly do so, and extend your finger for a long time, then remove your finger if it clings; this often happens; thus leave the arm, and let it be, and do not move it while in pain; have patience, and do not move it until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not closed and it bleeds, and the physician does not have medicines, tie the artery if it opens; for they pull back at the head; and close the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a slice of fistulae, and split it, and take one half and lay it until the next day; if it clings, that is good; if not, then cure it as we have said with powders that coagulate blood; and the coagulations are not caused by various conditions near the small place of the wound, nor by weakness in the bone's strength.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The vein of the vessel is pierced deeply to aid it so that blood flows from above and below the body because it is composed of the basilar and cephalic, as we have said; thus it behooves the surgeon to let himself be numb for the nerve underneath, and if he goes too far in, and finds the nerve, and it swells and becomes painful, and possibly cannot heal; this nerve is often opened many times, and if it does not open in any person due to its subtlety, then it must be sutured with a needle instrument; avoid injuring the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is no touch it the veuine, then they are l'a cauterisee.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The cephalic vein is pierced to aid it so that blood flows from the head and helps the eyes; and one must carefully suture by feeling for the olivaire groove or mirtin fossa, as this is the safest of all vessels since there are no nerves or arteries below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Nevertheless, it is necessary to take the lighter one, and nothing should be strained at first attempt, but try again; sometimes the limb swells in some people when attempted for the first time, but do not worry about this.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor. des sainies de ventouse	 And of suction cups

Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cuppings on the legs drain blood thoroughly, as they draw blood from all over the body; they are beneficial for old pains of the limbs and testicles, and bladder issues, and relieve the flowers; they are in place at the .ij. groins, and the .ij. ankles, and moreover, they weaken the body after long use and bring about swelling in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping is that you place it first empty, and then quickly, put on hastily, and move equally, and do not stop doing so, until you see there redness and swelling, and the bruise appears with dark blood; then remove, and reapply the cups, and take care in the arrangement of limbs, for there are some who have tender skin and clear pores: it is necessary to pierce once only, and make wide, somewhat deep cuts; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it should be pierced twice: the first time to facilitate the flow of thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very dry, it should be pierced a third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we only do so once at most.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want to draw much blood, perform frequently; and if the vessel is sharp, move slowly, and ensure that the veins are pierced quickly, and for those with thick and hard skin, who have narrow openings, apply oily ventosifiers: if it is so, violet oil, or almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is a wound, cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of amartine or balm of Gilead, or aniseed oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 If one whom you treat has a tender and broad chest, there is no need to put oil on it, but after ventosation with rose water or cold water, or blackthorn water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or any similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with much moisture should get up easily, or use myrtle water, and sumac, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those who have large swelling should rise from old wine, or blackthorn water, or anise decoction or chamomile infusion, or any similar substance; and they are not to be treated with a poultice before the bath nor after the bath but two hours afterwards; and they must not sleep after ventosation, as it is necessary for them to wash when ventosated and when needed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And beware if he who is sick feels colicky and his bowels are too agitated and inflamed; it must be that he consumes cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuces for refreshment, and similar items; mixed pinks, and chestnut charcoal, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And those who have a cold complexion should consume syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is half old and half new, along with small portions of foods such as young pears, berries, small birds, and geese; and on the day they undergo ventosation, they must drink more than eat. And it should be given to some patients triaicale or musk before or after ventilation to strengthen their main limbs; and liquefy their bowels but only those who are hot may consume them.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The suction cups that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and joints of the feet, gout, and on the abdebly swollen areas, haunches; for these limbs cannot be harmed by applying them anywhere, but only to draw blood from one member to another, as we place them on lumps when they are not healing; to remove the viscosity within the limb, as we apply suction cups on the abdomen and swollen areas to reduce the limb size; and it relieves pain, when there is congestion or stones, so by its attractive nature it may sometimes draw out the congestion, or remove the stone from its place; thus it acts when placed on the liver and joints of feet when viscosity is retained, and these suction cups are prepared empty to exude as much fluid; at times they are also used with fire, and at times filled with plain water, as in diseases causing heavy sweating, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot water or herb-infused water heated over coals.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with heat is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it has two pieces each half a palm wide at the front, and around the middle there is a small hole, as when pushing in an acupuncture needle, and they are made of reed or iron, placed forward so that it does not bother the patient on the limb; and in the middle there should be a barbed wire crossbar to hold a candle, with large and small sizes according to the diseases and the condition of those who take them; for children's cupping sets are different from adults', and thin as those of emaciated people compared to fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this is how you should place the cupping glass on the limb: take a wax candle or oil, and insert it into the bar across the crossbar within the cup, enspect that the light illuminates from the bottom of the cup so it does not burn the patient; then place the cup over the limb, positioned as we have said near the hole, and when you wish, let the steam go, and remove the cup; take the oil again as before, and start over often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the ventouse, therefore, which is prepared for the disease of pleurisy, it has no rod or tube and is made only when full of water, placed on the limb completely; this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Ventouses are made only for limbs where one cannot place ventouses due to smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and in naked areas of the body like ears or noses, and others; their quality is that when you find ventoses that are filled with soft clear water without impurps, take them; and put them into a bowl of soft clear water until they become well-formed, having nothing inside; then drain them of blood and ventose, then rub the limb so it turns red, and place the ventoses on it; when they are full and begin to sink, if there is a location where you can put a ventose, do so, as this is much more effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the limb and apply ice generously, then compress it; if the swelling is too much for the body without support, wring a linen cloth in cold water, and place over it until the swelling subsides; if there are multiple swellings, apply crushed vitriol or ointment, along with similar remedies, until they subside; or you can put moistened breads on the area around the limb, leaving them until they dry out and will now seal it; and if more is needed, take additional bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the swelling does not decrease, rub the limb with fresh blood or insert a needle until it draws out some fluid, and then place bandages on it; as soon as they feel the flow of blood, let them dry out; and when you see that they are oozing, powder with a bit of aloe vera and safflower paste, or ash, to stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These treatises are often necessary in the art of medicine, and they restore broken bones and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Learn from the wise thread that the foolish healer delves into this chapter, which is not found in any ancient books or letters read; and for this reason knowledge is strange on our land, for I have never come across a good one; and I know nothing unless through the wisdom of ancient books where I have studied so much that I have acquired knowledge from them, and by experimentation, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and abbreviated at the end, and shown clearly the forms of treatments that are employed, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say that the preamble of this book contains the essence and wisdom of its chapters, so those who are experienced apply their understanding to truth, allowing them to know and learn this noble art and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or twists or sprains occur in any part of the body, it is necessary to relieve the patient on both sides if nothing wholly covers them, as weaknesses of limbs, infants, or elders; and if the blood flow is not too thick, or too cold; and mix with cooling foods such as chilled broths, bread, and meat of birds and veal, do not drink wine, nor fatty meats, and do not fill yourself excessively with foods that make your veins full of blood until you have no doubt about an abscess or discharge of matter from the limb; then the patient will soon return to their normal state as they were accustomed.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient with foods that cause swelling or viscosity, such as boiled wheat, rice, eggs, beans, veal, chicken, fresh fish, and strong wine, along with similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	When with gradual dislocation, movement is soon followed by fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones from the old and decrepit cannot be well mended or joined according to their nature for limb strengthening, nor those also who are too tender, like children's bones; but do not care, reset with strong supports which hold together and join the limb as a whole until it is restored so that it was before; and not completely healed, and therefore one must nourish on fatty meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	by the bolejles Que c; If you say b: OU; ça finge t m and so et se ou n'ilz ne bon line: Ca: Jarn’s.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	When the break of the head is different from the break of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all types of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are fractures that go with rotation, and others by bending, as the length of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture accompanied by a tiny split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each way has its method and instrument for restoration according to what memory brings forth in that place; and it is known the bone break by how the joint is twisted, and openly broken quite far, and near squeezing of the hand; but if there is no twisting or touchable point, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no breakage unless it can have twisting, or fracture, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move your hand at all, but apply the medicines that come next and then gently hold it in place.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fracture that is in suspension, and are the two parts disjointed, they must now be set equally straight, just as with abscesses when it arises; and if an abscess swells up, leave none of its days until the abscess is soothed; then make it even again to movements you can move easily and sensibly, and know that the restoration for him is easier than those where there are pieces; then bind it, as it should be afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if the bone has broken pieces, when it is divided into two parts, whether hand or foot, or in your hand if it's a small member, or at both strings, or at one string and your hand; then set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you join them by all means to their places for movements you can move, and ensure by your craft there is no injury or pain to the patient; and place well both heads of bones in accordance with the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels severe pain in the arm if it seems to you that it is not well: so treat gently, and do not strain or press as those who cause abscesses and heat and shrinkage of the limb by their methods have often seen us do.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 When the limb is at risk, chastise the patient well so that they do not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning, or in any other manner; and ensure that the limb is secure enough that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when it feels no pain, then it is not at risk, and you should place it in a suitable position so that it feels no pain; and ensure that it is placed straightly, avoiding any twisting once restored; and the quality of the injured limb depends on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	; forment the c; The Chir, they so that is: corue me: the Juda de laise:n't. Do not to a. Preter. Here: theu said; in this t.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small limbs such as arms and legs: wrap them in soft and fine linen; for larger ones like thighs and legs: use a wide and strong bandage, as the wide bands encompass the entire large member evenly, without any unevenness; then apply light cotton wraps three or four turns according to the size of the limb, and tighten the hand on the whole bandage, then go above the fracture and loosen slightly so that the fracture moves away a little; and gradually soften the bandage bit by bit until you grasp a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage and turn back to the broken spot; then return to the part below the fracture and tighten moderately, not too hard or lightly as we have said in the first instruction above; then place linen or fabric strips between the bandages until they are all even, then go around with one layer of cloth, and then put well-made splints on top, unless there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 If there is swelling or an abscess, apply a soothing ointment for the abscess and remove the swelling, leaving it as such for several days; then bandage with neat strips of wide canvas, or wood used to make wedges, or palm fronds, shaped according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But it is necessary that the bandage put on the break should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and as long as required for limbs of small or large size; then wrap with the bandages in the same manner as you did for the first ligature, then above a thread at once, as in the first ligature over the fracture; tighter on top, gradually less so below. It is essential that the thread be of medium thickness and made of soft linen; because if the threads are too thick like those used by peasants to make their flax ropes, it is a great mistake, as the ligature cannot be even if they're too fine, and it must not have less than two inches space between each bandage.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is in pain from the shoulders of their extremities after being strained into place, then apply cotton or raw wool rags beneath them so they do not slip.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the head is broken, I will tell you the remedy for this below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not happen to pull out all the bones of a limb broken on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 When the limbs are large, it is not necessary to place them in splints unless after V days or VII, or more depending on the risk of abscesses occurring; and here is the manner of ancient stretches used for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take wheat flour that clings to the walls of a mill, mix it with plenty of egg white, and make this concoction, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, as this is the common method of stretching restoring fractures in various positions, especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of dressing to restore fractures and dislocations and twists: take pitch from pine resin and olive oil and onion juice and frankincense and gum arabic, each .x. Z.; myrrh and aloes, each .v. З.; camphor .viij. Z.; and make powder, mix with honey and plenty of water; if the person's complexion is hot, use this dressing as it has good composition and quickly heals broken bones, and works well for many individuals.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method of stretching for torsion: take muscat and violets in an amount of 50; myrrh and aloes in an amount of 90; acacia in an amount of 60; bolus armeniacum in an amount of 100, and finely grind it, then mix with water or plenty of egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way to reset dislocated joints and their bones from their places, soothes the pain arising, and when cutting into the bone, take new thread, and grind it with flour and cooked oil, and apply above the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 These plasters do not heal but are good to soothe of hot abscesses and properly alleviate the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of bandages that restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earthy wood leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to reset the healing of broken bones and reduce remaining abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of wormwood, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour; and grind them together with wine, and if the limb is swollen, apply it with juice of coriander or water, and there you rub it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way to treat more effectively than the first, when an abscess comes to heal the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of yarrow, and seed of flax, balm, mallows, wormwood, and without-juice; and flowers of violets and chamomile, all together in equal parts; then grind, and soak with saltwater or fresh water, or wine, depending on the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that one should not put anything other than a mixture of wax and oil on a broken limb for healing, except if it is too soft or too hard between two layers.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems like Galen suggests that on a broken limb for healing, one should use dry substances that are somewhat warm, such as myrrh, frankincense, and similar things, as we have mentioned before.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method for making an emplaster to soothe pain and inflammeblend of hairs from scalps, or feathers of birds, and wool alike, all finely ground, and made into a paste.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then gently rub again later on, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain or has lost their bone position; do not move them too early. If pain comes to the joint, or itching, feelings of restlessness or swelling occur, hurry up and reset it, remove the treatment immediately now; and apply a light ointer, and damp sponge in water, and immerse until pruritus subsides and the pain is relieved. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then place bandage on dry or moistened cloth, soaked in oil-rose or oil-balm, and tie it up with a nut (clothespin) as long as you are sure of high temperature; and rest the inflammation of the joint until pain subsides. Then reset cautiously, and a little treatment, but do not move too strongly as before; continue subtly until healthy again.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and warm and painful and swollen, and you need opiates and linen, then reset as before, similarly to how it was done initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 If nothing comes to the limb as we have said, do not reset it until after III days or IIII or V or VII; and never leave it unset for XX days, according to what one sees, as long as the breaker is sore, and approaches the joint above; then you securely fasten more than first, and encourage fleshing of the meat, as I have said before; and if you see that the place dries more than necessary, know that numbness will not come; so moisten it with hot water each time you reset, and do this every day, and ease a bit the ligature; thus numbness is prevented in the limb, and quickly restore its use as skilled physicians do, who return the joint correctly: it's bad practice, and I see nothing else but laziness and working properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many ways of breaks are, and various shapes, and the causes are distinguished. For there are breaks caused by the percussion of a sword, with the collarbone all through the bone up to the scapula which is underneath; and because of this such type of breakage is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword breaks through above and is called this type of fracture "absolute"; and there are wounds from these two large or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impacted blow, crack, neck bone fracture, or fall onto the spine, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fissure that reaches the tunic which lies below or above the bone, where the wound may be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that heals in the bone as delicate as with a hare's fur, and it is a small fissure, so this type of breakage is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made or by being struck by stones, or falling, or similar things, whereby the piece of bone goes inward, and the void above is like how a cauldron when placed over its stand; between the stone within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 This occurs more in those with wet bones, like children's skulls; and it happens in all these ways of fractures where small pieces are left loose as such; and I will speak about them on site.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all types of fractures by displacement underneath them, and the incisions on sinews, and by the corroded cartilage which is beneath.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	And they; (et d do not as he sonte t and ous le trementd; that are the ou pr* est: S, so it.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, beware of accidents to the patient, and if you see any bad accident such as vomiting bile, loss of understanding, extension, paleness, fever with chills, eyes protruding and turning red, and other similar dispositions, cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeful accident, and expect recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the suffering comes first to you, and it is in winter, then remove the bone before the fourteenth day when you can move it.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is like this, and you remove the bone within seven days, so that the tissue under the bone becomes corrupted, then come the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the cloth that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part this way: and take the head from the wounded patient's grip, and expose the skull in all ways possible, and over the wound area as much as you can, and if there is a bleeding flow revealed through exposing the bone or pus comes out, help it with what needs to be done, and that you fill the cavity of the wound with moistened rags soaked in oil rose; and allow the wound to rest until the discharge has subsided, and ensure bleeding is under control; then begin working around the bone to remove it, which is done according to the ways of operation: one way is that you cut at the narrow edge in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, pointed or made of iron; and when performing lightly, do not cut deeply into the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	If the bone is out of place and hardened, it must be approached on all sides, making indentations with tapered instruments without piercing beyond the outer layer of the bone, ensuring a margin or circle around which the point does not pass; thus several should be made so each finds its spot at the edge of the bone, having tapering points for all tests; these are the three forms of tapered points.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality of cutting around the fractured bone is to place one tapered point on the bone and turn it back and forth until you know that the bone has been pierced; then move the tapered point slightly, doing so all around, and with incisors cut the space between the perforations as subtly as possible, gently, as we have said, until you feel the bacteria on your hand or any of the tools that resemble pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 When you have pierced the bone and drained it, it is necessary to relieve the preparedness that has been held by the bone with any instrument similar to a chisel; but it must be more secure and finer than the other chisel; and if nothing of the small bones or scales remain, gently wash the wound with ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is what the Galen says, which is much wiser; and it holds strong, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you expose the bone part where the break opens up; and once you have exposed that part, then place atop the blade of this crescent-shaped incision tool, which has the following shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut too much from one side, and it is the hard part in two directions, so that the cutting tool is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet below, so that you chip the entire bone slightly, being careful of the tendon above; if it is near to the bone, chip the bone lightly, as not to harm or injure it.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce all the way through to the skin and is cut only from above, with small fragments remaining, you should attend to that sharpness again, and remove the scales with a fine razor in which various quantities must be used, so as to apply most appropriately to each location according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you approach from great heights, then proceed with more subtlety, and continue in this manner until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of these hair cutting and subtle fractures, it is necessary to adjust according to its direction; and this is something that cannot be simply restored for those who have studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the face is discovered, it is necessary that you take a linen bandage according to the amount of wound and moisten with oil rose, and place it on the wound; then take another padded bandage doubled in 2 or 3 layers, moisten with wine and oil rose, and place over the first bandage; do so as lightly as possible without burdening the face, then treat above the other joints, and do not stretch it more than to touch the wound only; leave like this for one day or two until the swelling is calmed, then remove it, and apply medicines such as roots of lilies, flour of dates, powdered incense, aristole, and similar things; from these things make a powder, and place on wound, and therein administer other medicines without irritating the skin; ensure that the wound remains clean, not leaving oil or causing swelling, because when bowels gather under the cerebral linen, they can cause harm and lead to great suffering; for when something mordant is placed on the face, it becomes numb.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, should any unfortunate event occur to the patient as we have mentioned, it is doubtful and uncertain.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If darkness only comes when the medicine is applied and its virtue must be tested, you should take a part of honey, three parts of rose oil and rosin in cloth, and apply it to the wound; then treat as needed until it heals completely.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two pieces of the neck above are broken, or one by another, for they are bones; and the underside is cartilaginous, does not break but rather bend or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, you must sew your small thumb or earlobe and place the tear inside your index finger, and along the edge nearer to the palm, until it heals according to its natural shape; do this gently, ensuring the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose and cannot bring the finger to its place, it is appropriate that you put a little bit of grease on the top of a small stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the tear is in two parts, repeat as before and attempt to restore it on the first day; if not possible, try again after seven days or until swelling subsides, then apply honey-infused linen strips over the wound if the tear is on one side.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you dress it with another kind of cloth on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be thick enough to fill up the openings in the skin.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And each healer says one must grease the wounds with butter, and change it every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It seems to me not certain that this is right, but it must be greased with a mixture of oil and egg yolk, and powdered flour; then leave the wound until the bone has healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	At no time should you place goose feathers near the tent openings, and if they are in a certain sleeve, and there is a breach, and it blows on the sick person; do as follows:
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the patient while you work on it, then put some grease or cotton wool in oil roseate, or a small portion of diacron.

Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.
